--- Commit Message ---
LU-12187 lfs: add EC setstripe support with k+m notation

Add support for Erasure Coding (EC) layouts in lfs
setstripe using simple "k+m" notation where k is data
stripe count and 'm' is parity stripe count
(must be <= min('k', 4)) that make up the RAID Set
geometry.

When --ec is specified, an EC parity mirror is
automatically created that matches the data mirror's
extent structure. The --ec option can appear anywhere
in the command line.

EC Inheritance Rules:
- Single --ec applies to all components in the parity
  mirror
- Multiple --ec values inherit forward: each applies to
  its component and subsequent components until replaced
  by another --ec
- The first --ec also applies to any earlier components
  (backward inheritance)

EC Stripe Count Adjustment:
- The EC parity data count (k) is capped at the data
  component's stripe count (-c). If the component's
  stripe count is less than k, the EC data count is
  automatically reduced to match.
- The component's -c value takes precedence; the --ec
  data count only sets the upper bound for parity.
- Example: -E 128M -c 4 -E -1 -c 16 --ec 8+2
  creates EC 4+2 for the first component (stripe_count
  4 < k=8, so k is reduced) and EC 8+2 for the second
  (stripe_count 16 > k=8, so k=8 is used as-is)

Usage examples:
  # Single component with EC(8+2)
  lfs setstripe -E -1 -c 8 --ec 8+2 /mnt/lustre/file

  # Order independent (--ec can appear anywhere)
  lfs setstripe --ec 8+2 -E -1 -c 8 /mnt/lustre/file

  # Multiple components, single EC spec (both get EC 8+2)
  lfs setstripe -E 1G -E -1 --ec 8+2 /mnt/lustre/file

  # Different EC for different components
  lfs setstripe -E 1G --ec 4+2 -E -1 --ec 8+2
    /mnt/lustre/file

  # EC inheritance with holes
  lfs setstripe -E 1G --ec 4+2 -E 512M -E -1 --ec 8+2
    /mnt/lustre/file

  # Long form option
  lfs setstripe --ec-stripe-count 4+2 -E -1
    /mnt/lustre/file

A new testlist sanity-ec is added to exercise the new
setstripe options.

Further, tombstones were added to guarantee
"llite.*.enable_erasure_coding" is enabled by default and
setting the environment variable "LFS_EC_OK=yes" is no
longer needed before 2.18.

Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity-ec
Signed-off-by: Patrick Farrell <pfarrell@whamcloud.com>

## Summary

**Fix Applied:** Removed the unused variable `mirror_id` from the `llapi_layout_merge()` function in `lustre/utils/liblustreapi_layout.c`.

**Rationale:** 
The patch added EC (Erasure Coding) support to Lustre's file striping functionality. In the `llapi_layout_merge()` function at line 3585, a local variable `uint32_t mirror_id;` was declared but never used anywhere in the function. Since the code is compiled with `-Werror=unused-variable`, this caused a compilation error.

The variable declaration was likely left over from development or was intended for future use but never actually implemented. Removing it resolves the compilation error without affecting any functionality, as the variable was never referenced in the code.

Here's summary of my changes:
Excellent! All three call sites have been fixed.

## Summary

**Fix Applied:** Removed the extra fourth argument from all three calls to `create_ec_parity_mirror()`.

**Rationale:** 

The patch introduced a function `create_ec_parity_mirror()` that accepts exactly 3 parameters:
1. `struct llapi_layout *layout` - the layout to add EC parity mirror to
2. `struct ec_spec *ec_specs` - array of EC specifications
3. `int ec_spec_count` - number of EC specifications

However, the function was being called with a fourth argument in three locations:
- Line 4918: called with extra argument `0`
- Line 5234: called with extra argument `0`  
- Line 5273: called with extra argument `lsa.lsa_comp_count`

This fourth argument doesn't match the function signature and caused compilation errors. The fix removes this extraneous argument from all three call sites, making them match the function declaration. The function itself doesn't need this extra parameter as it internally counts components and applies EC specifications based on the `ec_specs` array.
